<p><b>Maria Theresa Walburga Amalia Christina</b><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Maria Theresia</i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">[maˈʀiːa teˈʀeːzi̯a]</a></span>; 13&#160;May 1717 – 29&#160;November 1780) was the only female ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg dominions</a> and the last of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a>. She was the sovereign of <a href="/wiki/Archduchy_of_Austria" title="Archduchy of Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Croatia_(Habsburg)" title="Kingdom of Croatia (Habsburg)">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mantua" title="Mantua">Mantua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia_and_Lodomeria" title="Kingdom of Galicia and Lodomeria">Lodomeria and Galicia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands#Austrian_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Austrian Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parma" title="Parma">Parma</a>. By marriage, she was <a href="/wiki/Duchess_of_Lorraine" title="Duchess of Lorraine" class="mw-redirect">Duchess of Lorraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchess_of_Tuscany" title="Grand Duchess of Tuscany" class="mw-redirect">Grand Duchess of Tuscany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empress" title="Holy Roman Empress" class="mw-redirect">Holy Roman Empress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>She started her 40-year reign when her father, <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Charles VI</a>, died in October 1740. Charles&#160;VI paved the way for her accession with the <a href="/wiki/Pragmatic_Sanction_of_1713" title="Pragmatic Sanction of 1713">Pragmatic Sanction of 1713</a> and spent his entire reign securing it.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon the death of her father, <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Saxony" title="Electorate of Saxony">Saxony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Bavaria" title="Electorate of Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a> all repudiated the sanction they had recognised during his lifetime. Prussia proceeded to invade the affluent Habsburg province of <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>, sparking a nine-year conflict known as the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a>, and subsequently conquered it. Maria Theresa would later unsuccessfully try to reconquer Silesia during the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>.</p>
<p>Maria Theresa and her husband, <a href="/wiki/Francis_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Francis I, Holy Roman Emperor">Francis I, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, had sixteen children, including <a href="/wiki/Marie_Antoinette" title="Marie Antoinette">the Queen of France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Carolina_of_Austria" title="Maria Carolina of Austria">the Queen of Naples and Sicily</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Amalia_of_Austria" title="Archduchess Maria Amalia of Austria">the Duchess of Parma</a> and two Holy Roman Emperors, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Leopold II, Holy Roman Emperor">Leopold II</a>. Out of the sixteen, nine or ten of them did not make it to adulthood. She had eleven daughters, ten of which were named Marie, and five sons. Though she was expected to cede power to Francis and Joseph, both of whom were officially her co-rulers in Austria and Bohemia,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Maria Theresa was the absolute sovereign who ruled by the counsel of her advisers.<sup id="cite_ref-Kann.2C_157_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kann.2C_157-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> She criticised and disapproved of many of Joseph's actions. Although she is considered to have been intellectually inferior to both Joseph and Leopold,<sup id="cite_ref-Kann.2C_157_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kann.2C_157-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Maria Theresa understood the importance of her public persona and was able to simultaneously evoke both esteem and affection from her subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning.2C_67_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning.2C_67-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Maria Theresa <a href="/wiki/Promulgation" title="Promulgation">promulgated</a> financial and educational reforms, with the assistance of <a href="/wiki/Count_Friedrich_Wilhelm_von_Haugwitz" title="Count Friedrich Wilhelm von Haugwitz">Count Friedrich Wilhelm von Haugwitz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gerard_van_Swieten" title="Gerard van Swieten">Gerard van Swieten</a>, promoted commerce and the development of agriculture, and reorganised Austria's ramshackle military, all of which strengthened Austria's international standing. However, she refused to allow <a href="/wiki/Religious_toleration" title="Religious toleration" class="mw-redirect">religious toleration</a><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> and contemporaneous travellers thought her regime was bigoted and superstitious.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> As a young monarch who fought two dynastic wars, she believed that her cause should be the cause of her subjects, but in her later years she would believe that their cause must be hers.<sup id="cite_ref-Russell_Richards_Treasure.2C_410_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Russell_Richards_Treasure.2C_410-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2>Contents</h2>
</div>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_and_background">Birth and background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Birth and background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresa,_age_3.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Maria_Theresa%2C_age_3.jpeg/220px-Maria_Theresa%2C_age_3.jpeg" width="220" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Maria_Theresa%2C_age_3.jpeg/330px-Maria_Theresa%2C_age_3.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Maria_Theresa%2C_age_3.jpeg/440px-Maria_Theresa%2C_age_3.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1261" data-file-height="1530" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresa,_age_3.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Three-year-old Maria Theresa in the gardens of <a href="/wiki/Hofburg_Palace" title="Hofburg Palace">Hofburg Palace</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The second and eldest surviving child of <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor Charles VI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Christine_of_Brunswick-Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="Elisabeth Christine of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel">Elisabeth Christine of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel</a>, Archduchess Maria Theresa was born early in the morning of 13&#160;May 1717, at the <a href="/wiki/Hofburg_Palace" title="Hofburg Palace">Hofburg Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, shortly after the death of her elder brother, Archduke Leopold, and was baptised on that same evening. The dowager empresses, her aunt <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmine_Amalia_of_Brunswick-L%C3%BCneburg" title="Wilhelmine Amalia of Brunswick-Lüneburg">Wilhelmine Amalia of Brunswick-Lüneburg</a> and grandmother <a href="/wiki/Eleonor_Magdalene_of_the_Palatinate-Neuburg" title="Eleonor Magdalene of the Palatinate-Neuburg" class="mw-redirect">Eleonor Magdalene of the Palatinate-Neuburg</a>, were her godmothers.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Most descriptions of her baptism stress that the infant was carried ahead of her cousins, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Josepha_of_Austria" title="Maria Josepha of Austria">Maria Josepha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maria_Amalia_of_Austria" title="Maria Amalia of Austria">Maria Amalia</a>, the daughters of Charles VI's elder brother and predecessor, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph I, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph I</a>, before the eyes of their mother, Wilhelmine Amalia. It was clear that Maria Theresa would outrank them, even though their grandfather, <a href="/wiki/Leopold_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Leopold I, Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor Leopold I</a>, had his sons sign the <a href="/wiki/Mutual_Pact_of_Succession" title="Mutual Pact of Succession">Mutual Pact of Succession</a>, which gave precedence to the daughters of the elder brother.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Her father was the only surviving male member of the House of Habsburg and hoped for a son who would prevent the extinction of his dynasty and succeed him. Thus, the birth of Maria Theresa was a great disappointment to him and the people of Vienna; Charles never managed to overcome this feeling.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Maria Theresa replaced Maria Josepha as <a href="/wiki/Heiress_presumptive" title="Heiress presumptive" class="mw-redirect">heiress presumptive</a> to the Habsburg realms the moment she was born; Charles VI had issued the <a href="/wiki/Pragmatic_Sanction_of_1713" title="Pragmatic Sanction of 1713">Pragmatic Sanction of 1713</a> which had placed his nieces behind his own daughters in the line of succession.<sup id="cite_ref-Ingrao.2C_129_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ingrao.2C_129-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Charles sought the other European powers' approval for disinheriting his nieces. They exacted harsh terms: in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Vienna_(1731)" title="Treaty of Vienna (1731)">Treaty of Vienna (1731)</a>, Great Britain demanded that Austria abolish the <a href="/wiki/Ostend_Company" title="Ostend Company">Ostend Company</a> in return for its recognition of the Pragmatic Sanction.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In total, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Saxony" title="Electorate of Saxony">Saxony</a>-<a href="/wiki/Polish-Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">United Provinces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venice</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-C37_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C37-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">States of the Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-C37_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C37-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Brittanica1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brittanica1-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-C37_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C37-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Brittanica1_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brittanica1-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Savoy-Sardinia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Brittanica1_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brittanica1-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bavaria" title="History of Bavaria">Bavaria</a><sup id="cite_ref-Brittanica1_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brittanica1-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Diet_of_the_Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Diet of the Holy Roman Empire" class="mw-redirect">Diet of the Holy Roman Empire</a><sup id="cite_ref-Brittanica1_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brittanica1-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> recognised the sanction. France, Spain, Saxony-Poland, Bavaria and Prussia later reneged.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andreas_Moeller_-_Erzherzogin_Maria_Theresia_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Andreas_Moeller_-_Erzherzogin_Maria_Theresia_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum.jpg/220px-Andreas_Moeller_-_Erzherzogin_Maria_Theresia_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum.jpg" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Andreas_Moeller_-_Erzherzogin_Maria_Theresia_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum.jpg/330px-Andreas_Moeller_-_Erzherzogin_Maria_Theresia_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/eb/Andreas_Moeller_-_Erzherzogin_Maria_Theresia_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="388" data-file-height="479" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andreas_Moeller_-_Erzherzogin_Maria_Theresia_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Archduchess Maria Theresa in 1729,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Andreas_M%C3%B8ller_(portrait_painter)" title="Andreas Møller (portrait painter)" class="mw-redirect">Andreas Möller</a>. The flowers which she carries in the uplifted folds of her dress represent her fertility and expectations to bear children in adulthood.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Little more than a year after her birth, Maria Theresa was joined by a sister, <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Anna_of_Austria_(1718%E2%80%931744)" title="Archduchess Maria Anna of Austria (1718–1744)" class="mw-redirect">Maria Anna</a>, and another one, named <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Amalia_of_Austria_(1724-1730)" title="Archduchess Maria Amalia of Austria (1724-1730)">Maria Amalia</a>, was born in 1724.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The portraits of the imperial family show that Maria Theresa resembled Elisabeth Christine and Maria Anna.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The Prussian ambassador noted that she had large blue eyes, fair hair with a slight tinge of red, a wide mouth and a notably strong body.<sup id="cite_ref-Russell_Richards_Treasure.2C_410_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Russell_Richards_Treasure.2C_410-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Neither her parents nor her grandparents were closely related to each other, making Maria Theresa one of few members of the House of Habsburg who was not inbred.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Maria Theresa was a serious and reserved child who enjoyed singing and archery.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> She was barred from horse riding by her father, but she would later learn the basics for the sake of her <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_Hungarian_monarch" title="Coronation of the Hungarian monarch">Hungarian coronation ceremony</a>. The imperial family staged opera productions, often conducted by Charles&#160;VI, in which she relished participating.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Her education was overseen by <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuits</a>. Contemporaries thought her <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> to be quite good, but in all else, the Jesuits did not educate her well. Her spelling and punctuation were unconventional and she lacked the formal manner and speech which had characterized her Habsburg predecessors.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Maria Theresa developed a close relationship with <a href="/wiki/Marie_Karoline_von_Fuchs-Mollard" title="Marie Karoline von Fuchs-Mollard">Countess Marie Karoline von Fuchs-Mollard</a>, who taught her etiquette. She was educated in drawing, painting, music and dancing – the disciplines which would have prepared her for the role of <a href="/wiki/Queen_consort" title="Queen consort">queen consort</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahan.2C_22_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahan.2C_22-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Her father allowed her to attend meetings of the council from the age of 14 but never discussed the affairs of state with her.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris.2C_28_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morris.2C_28-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Even though he had spent the last decades of his life securing Maria Theresa's inheritance, Charles always expected a son and never prepared his daughter for her future role as sovereign.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Browning.2C_37_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning.2C_37-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresa_and_Francis_Wedding_Breakfast_by_Martin_van_Meytens_ca_1736.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Maria_Theresa_and_Francis_Wedding_Breakfast_by_Martin_van_Meytens_ca_1736.jpg/220px-Maria_Theresa_and_Francis_Wedding_Breakfast_by_Martin_van_Meytens_ca_1736.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Maria_Theresa_and_Francis_Wedding_Breakfast_by_Martin_van_Meytens_ca_1736.jpg/330px-Maria_Theresa_and_Francis_Wedding_Breakfast_by_Martin_van_Meytens_ca_1736.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Maria_Theresa_and_Francis_Wedding_Breakfast_by_Martin_van_Meytens_ca_1736.jpg/440px-Maria_Theresa_and_Francis_Wedding_Breakfast_by_Martin_van_Meytens_ca_1736.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="471" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresa_and_Francis_Wedding_Breakfast_by_Martin_van_Meytens_ca_1736.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maria Theresa and Francis Stephen at their <a href="/wiki/Wedding_breakfast" title="Wedding breakfast">wedding breakfast</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Martin_van_Meytens" title="Martin van Meytens">Martin van Meytens</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The question of Maria Theresa's marriage was raised early in her childhood. She was first engaged to be married to <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9opold_Cl%C3%A9ment,_Hereditary_Prince_of_Lorraine" title="Léopold Clément, Hereditary Prince of Lorraine">Leopold Clement of Lorraine</a>, who was supposed to visit Vienna and meet the Archduchess in 1723. However, news reached Vienna that he had died of <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Leopold Clement's younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Francis_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Francis I, Holy Roman Emperor">Francis Stephen</a>, was invited to Vienna. Even though Francis Stephen was his favourite candidate for Maria Theresa's hand,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> the Emperor considered other possibilities. Religious differences prevented him from arranging his daughter's marriage to the Calvinist prince <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II_of_Prussia" title="Frederick II of Prussia" class="mw-redirect">Frederick of Prussia</a>. In 1725, he betrothed her to <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">Charles of Spain</a> and her sister, Maria Anna, to <a href="/wiki/Philip,_Duke_of_Parma" title="Philip, Duke of Parma">Philip of Spain</a>. However, other European powers compelled him to renounce the pact he had made with the Queen of Spain, <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Farnese" title="Elisabeth Farnese">Elisabeth Farnese</a>, as the marriage of heirs to the thrones of Spain and Austria would have destroyed the <a href="/wiki/European_balance_of_power" title="European balance of power">European balance of power</a>. Maria Theresa, who had become close to Francis Stephen, was relieved.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Francis Stephen remained at the imperial court until 1729, when he ascended the throne of Lorraine,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> but was not formally promised Maria Theresa's hand until 31 January 1736, during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Polish_Succession" title="War of the Polish Succession">War of the Polish Succession</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Louis_XV_of_France" title="Louis XV of France">Louis XV of France</a> demanded that Maria Theresa's fiancé surrender his ancestral <a href="/wiki/Lorraine_(province)" title="Lorraine (province)" class="mw-redirect">Duchy of Lorraine</a> to accommodate his father-in-law, <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_I" title="Stanisław I">Stanisław I</a>, who had been deposed as King of Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Francis Stephen was to receive the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Tuscany" title="Grand Duchy of Tuscany">Grand Duchy of Tuscany</a> upon the death of childless Grand Duke <a href="/wiki/Gian_Gastone_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Gian Gastone de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Gian Gastone de' Medici</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> The couple were married on 12 February 1736.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Duchess of Lorraine's love for her husband was strong and possessive.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The letters she sent to him shortly before their marriage expressed her eagerness to see him; his letters, on the other hand, were stereotyped and formal.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> She was very jealous of her husband and his infidelity was the greatest problem of their marriage,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Maria_Wilhelmina_von_Neipperg" title="Maria Wilhelmina von Neipperg">Maria Wilhelmina, Princess of Auersperg</a>, as his best-known mistress.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Upon Gian Gastone's death on 9 July 1737, Francis Stephen ceded Lorraine and became Grand Duke of Tuscany. In 1738, Charles&#160;VI sent the young couple to make their formal entry into Tuscany. A triumphal arch was erected at the Porta Galla in celebration, where it remains today. Their stay in <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a> was brief. Charles&#160;VI soon recalled them, as he feared he might die while his heiress was miles away in Tuscany.<sup id="cite_ref-C26_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C26-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> In the summer of 1738, Austria suffered defeats during the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1735%E2%80%931739)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1735–1739)" class="mw-redirect">Russo-Turkish War</a>. The Turks reversed Austrian gains in <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_Eyalet" title="Bosnia Eyalet">Bosnia</a>. The Viennese rioted at the cost of the war. Francis Stephen was popularly despised, as he was thought to be a cowardly French spy.<sup id="cite_ref-C26_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C26-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> The war was concluded the next year with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Belgrade" title="Treaty of Belgrade">Treaty of Belgrade</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accession">Accession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Accession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oath_of_Fealty_to_Maria_Theresa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Oath_of_Fealty_to_Maria_Theresa.jpg/220px-Oath_of_Fealty_to_Maria_Theresa.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Oath_of_Fealty_to_Maria_Theresa.jpg/330px-Oath_of_Fealty_to_Maria_Theresa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Oath_of_Fealty_to_Maria_Theresa.jpg/440px-Oath_of_Fealty_to_Maria_Theresa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3268" data-file-height="2089" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oath_of_Fealty_to_Maria_Theresa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maria Theresa's procession through the <a href="/wiki/Graben,_Vienna" title="Graben, Vienna">Graben</a>, 22 November 1740. The pregnant queen is on way to hear High Mass at <a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Cathedral,_Vienna" title="St. Stephen's Cathedral, Vienna">St. Stephen's Cathedral</a> before receiving homage.<sup id="cite_ref-S207_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S207-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Charles VI died on 20 October 1740, probably of mushroom poisoning. He had ignored the advice of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Eugene_of_Savoy" title="Prince Eugene of Savoy">Prince Eugene of Savoy</a> who had urged him to concentrate on filling the treasury and equipping the army rather than on acquiring signatures of fellow monarchs.<sup id="cite_ref-Ingrao.2C_129_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ingrao.2C_129-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The Emperor, who spent his entire reign securing the Pragmatic Sanction, left Austria in an impoverished state, bankrupted by the recent Turkish war and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Polish_Succession" title="War of the Polish Succession">War of the Polish Succession</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> the treasury contained only 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_gulden" title="Austro-Hungarian gulden">florins</a>, which were claimed by his widow.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris.2C_47_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morris.2C_47-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The army numbered only 80,000&#160;men, most of whom had not been paid in months; they were nevertheless remarkably loyal and devoted to their new sovereign.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Maria Theresa found herself in a difficult situation. She did not know enough about matters of state and she was unaware of the weakness of her father's ministers. She decided to rely on her father's advice to retain his councillors and defer to her husband, whom she considered to be more experienced, on other matters. Both decisions, though natural, later gave cause for regret. Ten years later, Maria Theresa recalled in her <i>Political Testament</i> the circumstances under which she had ascended: "I found myself without money, without credit, without army, without experience and knowledge of my own and finally, also without any counsel because each one of them at first wanted to wait and see how things would develop."<sup id="cite_ref-Browning.2C_37_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning.2C_37-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>She dismissed the possibility that other countries might try to seize her territories and immediately started ensuring the imperial dignity for herself;<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> since a woman could not be elected <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Empress</a>, Maria Theresa wanted to secure the imperial office for her husband. However, Francis Stephen did not possess enough land or rank within the Holy Roman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> In order to make him eligible for the imperial throne and to enable him to vote in the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_election" title="Imperial election">imperial elections</a> as <a href="/wiki/Elector_of_Bohemia" title="Elector of Bohemia" class="mw-redirect">elector of Bohemia</a> (which she couldn't because of her sex), Maria Theresa made Francis Stephen <a href="/wiki/Coregency" title="Coregency">co-ruler</a> of the Austrian and Bohemian lands on 21&#160;November 1740.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> However, it took more than a year for the Diet of Hungary to accept Francis Stephen as co-ruler.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning.2C_38_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning.2C_38-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite her love for him and his position as co-ruler, Maria Theresa never allowed her husband to decide matters of state and often dismissed him from council meetings when they disagreed.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The first display of the new queen's authority was the formal act of <a href="/wiki/Homage_(medieval)" title="Homage (medieval)" class="mw-redirect">homage</a> of the Lower Austrian Estates to her on 22&#160;November 1740. It was an elaborate public event which served as a formal recognition and legitimation of her accession. The <a href="/wiki/Oath_of_fealty" title="Oath of fealty" class="mw-redirect">oath of fealty</a> to Maria Theresa was taken on the same day in Hofburg.<sup id="cite_ref-S207_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S207-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_the_Austrian_Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: War of the Austrian Succession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M%C3%A1ria_Ter%C3%A9zia_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_Szent_M%C3%A1rton_sz%C3%A9kesegyh%C3%A1zban.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/M%C3%A1ria_Ter%C3%A9zia_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_Szent_M%C3%A1rton_sz%C3%A9kesegyh%C3%A1zban.jpg/220px-M%C3%A1ria_Ter%C3%A9zia_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_Szent_M%C3%A1rton_sz%C3%A9kesegyh%C3%A1zban.jpg" width="220" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/M%C3%A1ria_Ter%C3%A9zia_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_Szent_M%C3%A1rton_sz%C3%A9kesegyh%C3%A1zban.jpg/330px-M%C3%A1ria_Ter%C3%A9zia_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_Szent_M%C3%A1rton_sz%C3%A9kesegyh%C3%A1zban.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/M%C3%A1ria_Ter%C3%A9zia_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_Szent_M%C3%A1rton_sz%C3%A9kesegyh%C3%A1zban.jpg/440px-M%C3%A1ria_Ter%C3%A9zia_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_Szent_M%C3%A1rton_sz%C3%A9kesegyh%C3%A1zban.jpg 2x" data-file-width="529" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M%C3%A1ria_Ter%C3%A9zia_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_a_Szent_M%C3%A1rton_sz%C3%A9kesegyh%C3%A1zban.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maria Theresa being crowned Queen of Hungary, <a href="/wiki/St._Martin%27s_Cathedral,_Bratislava" title="St. Martin's Cathedral, Bratislava">St. Martin's Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Pressburg</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Immediately after her accession, a number of European sovereigns who had recognised Maria Theresa as heiress broke their promises; Queen Elisabeth of Spain and Elector <a href="/wiki/Charles_VII,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VII, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles Albert of Bavaria</a>, married to Maria Theresa's deprived cousin Maria Amalia and supported by Empress Wilhelmine Amalia, wanted portions of her inheritance.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris.2C_47_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morris.2C_47-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Maria Theresa secured the recognition of King <a href="/wiki/Charles_Emmanuel_III_of_Sardinia" title="Charles Emmanuel III of Sardinia">Charles Emmanuel III of Sardinia</a>, who hadn't accepted the Pragmatic Sanction during her father's lifetime, in November 1740.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning.2C_38_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning.2C_38-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December, King <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II_of_Prussia" title="Frederick II of Prussia" class="mw-redirect">Frederick II of Prussia</a> invaded the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Silesia" title="Duchy of Silesia">Duchy of Silesia</a> and requested that Maria Theresa cede it, threatening to join her enemies if she refused. Maria Theresa decided to fight for the mineral-rich province.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Frederick even offered a compromise: he would defend Maria Theresa's rights if she agreed to cede him at least a part of Silesia. Francis Stephen was inclined to consider such an arrangement, but the Queen and her advisers were not, fearing that any violation of the Pragmatic Sanction would invalidate the entire document.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Maria Theresa's firmness soon assured Francis Stephen that they should fight for Silesia<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> and she was confident that she would retain "the jewel of the House of Austria".<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The invasion of Silesia by Frederick was the start of a lifelong enmity; she referred to him as "that evil man".<sup id="cite_ref-Holborn.2C_218_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holborn.2C_218-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:30em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>She has, as you well know, a terrible hatred for France, with which nation it is most difficult for her to keep on good terms, but she controls this passion except when she thinks to her advantage to display it. She detests Your Majesty, but acknowledges your ability. She cannot forget the loss of Silesia, nor her grief over the soldiers she lost in wars with you.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>Prussian ambassador's letter to <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>As Austria was short of experienced military commanders, Maria Theresa released <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Reinhard_von_Neipperg" title="Wilhelm Reinhard von Neipperg">Marshall Neipperg</a>, who had been imprisoned by her father for his poor performance in the Turkish War.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Neipperg took command of the Austrian troops in March. The Austrians suffered a crushing defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mollwitz" title="Battle of Mollwitz">Battle of Mollwitz</a> in April 1741.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> France drew up a plan to partition Austria between Prussia, Bavaria, Saxony and Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Louis_Auguste_Fouquet,_duc_de_Belle-Isle" title="Charles Louis Auguste Fouquet, duc de Belle-Isle">Marshall Belle-Isle</a> joined Frederick at Olmütz. Vienna was in a panic, as none of Maria Theresa's advisors expected France to betray them. Francis Stephen urged Maria Theresa to reach a <a href="/wiki/Rapprochement" title="Rapprochement">rapprochement</a> with Prussia, as did Great Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Maria Theresa reluctantly agreed to negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-C8_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C8-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Contrary to all expectations, a significant amount of support for the young Queen came from Hungary.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Her coronation as queen of Hungary took place in <a href="/wiki/St._Martin%27s_Cathedral,_Bratislava" title="St. Martin's Cathedral, Bratislava">St. Martin's Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pressburg" title="Pressburg" class="mw-redirect">Pressburg</a> on 25 June 1741 after she had spent months honing the equestrian skills necessary for the ceremony and negotiating with the <a href="/wiki/Diet_(assembly)" title="Diet (assembly)">Diet</a>. To appease those who considered her sex to be the most serious obstacle, Maria Theresa assumed masculine titles. Thus, in nomenclature, Maria Theresa was archduke and king; normally, however, she was styled as queen. No 18th-century commentary saw this crossing of gendered titles as inappropriate or impossible.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_van_Meytens_-_Cesarica_Marija_Terezija.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Martin_van_Meytens_-_Cesarica_Marija_Terezija.jpg/220px-Martin_van_Meytens_-_Cesarica_Marija_Terezija.jpg" width="220" height="339" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Martin_van_Meytens_-_Cesarica_Marija_Terezija.jpg/330px-Martin_van_Meytens_-_Cesarica_Marija_Terezija.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Martin_van_Meytens_-_Cesarica_Marija_Terezija.jpg/440px-Martin_van_Meytens_-_Cesarica_Marija_Terezija.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1038" data-file-height="1600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_van_Meytens_-_Cesarica_Marija_Terezija.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maria Theresa, by <a href="/wiki/Martin_van_Meytens" title="Martin van Meytens">Martin van Meytens</a> 1742</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By July, attempts at conciliation had completely collapsed. Maria Theresa's ally, the Elector of Saxony, now became her enemy<sup id="cite_ref-Cr75_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cr75-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> and George&#160;II declared the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Brunswick-L%C3%BCneburg" title="Electorate of Brunswick-Lüneburg">Electorate of Brunswick-Lüneburg</a> to be neutral.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The Queen was once again in need of help from Hungary. In order to obtain it, she granted favours to the Hungarian noblemen and flattered them without conceding to all of their demands. She had already won their support when she appeared in Pressburg in September 1741, hoping to persuade the Diet to call a mass <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> and recognise Francis Stephen as co-ruler. Upon achieving both goals, she showed her gift for theatrical displays by triumphantly holding her son and heir, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph</a>, before the Diet, thereby gaining sympathy of the noblemen.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning.2C_67_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning.2C_67-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1741, the Austrian authorities informed Maria Theresa that Bohemian populace would prefer Charles Albert to her as sovereign. Maria Theresa, desperate and burdened by pregnancy, wrote plaintively to her sister: "I don't know if a town will remain to me for my delivery."<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> She bitterly vowed to spare nothing and no one to defend her kingdom when she wrote to the Bohemian chancellor, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Kinsky" title="Philip Kinsky" class="mw-redirect">Count Philip Kinsky</a>: "My mind is made up. We must put everything at stake to save Bohemia."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> On 26&#160;October, the Elector of Bavaria captured <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> and declared himself <a href="/wiki/King_of_Bohemia" title="King of Bohemia" class="mw-redirect">King of Bohemia</a>. Maria Theresa, then in Hungary, wept on learning of the loss of Bohemia.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Charles Albert was unanimously elected Holy Roman Emperor on 24&#160;January 1742. The Archduchess, who regarded the election as a catastrophe,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> caught her enemies unprepared by insisting on a winter campaign;<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> the same day he was elected emperor, Austrian troops under <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Andreas_von_Khevenh%C3%BCller" title="Ludwig Andreas von Khevenhüller">Ludwig Andreas von Khevenhüller</a> captured <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, Charles Albert's capital.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Breslau" title="Treaty of Breslau">Treaty of Breslau</a> of June 1742 ended hostilities between Austria and Prussia. The Archduchess soon made the recovery of Bohemia her priority.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> French troops fled Bohemia in the winter of the same year. On 12&#160;May 1743, Maria Theresa had herself crowned Queen of Bohemia in <a href="/wiki/St._Vitus_Cathedral" title="St. Vitus Cathedral">St. Vitus Cathedral</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Prussia became anxious at Austrian advances on the Rhine frontier, and Frederick sacked Prague in August 1744. The French plans fell apart when Charles Albert died in January 1745. The French overran the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Netherlands" title="Austrian Netherlands">Austrian Netherlands</a> in May.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Francis Stephen was elected Holy Roman Emperor on 13 September 1745. Prussia recognised Francis as emperor, and Maria Theresa once again recognised the loss of Silesia by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Breslau" title="Treaty of Breslau">Treaty of Breslau</a> in December 1745.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The war dragged on for another three years, with fighting in northern Italy and the Austrian Netherlands. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1748)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)">Treaty of Aix-La-Chapelle</a>, which concluded the eight-year conflict, recognised Prussia's possession of Silesia and Maria Theresa ceded the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Parma" title="Duchy of Parma">Duchy of Parma</a> to Philip of Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seven_Years.27_War">Seven Years' War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Seven Years' War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg/220px-Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg/330px-Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg/440px-Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="377" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The battle of Kolin, 1757</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frederick of Prussia's invasion of Saxony in August 1756 began the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>. Empress Maria Theresa and <a href="/wiki/Wenzel_Anton,_Prince_of_Kaunitz-Rietberg" title="Wenzel Anton, Prince of Kaunitz-Rietberg">Kaunitz</a> wished to exit the war with possession of Silesia.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Austria was aligned with France and Russia, Great Britain with Prussia and Portugal. Giving Austria huge subsidies came back to haunt France. It could not bolster defences in <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>; the British easily captured <a href="/wiki/Louisbourg" title="Louisbourg">Louisbourg</a> in 1758, and went on to conquer all of New France.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Ulysses_Browne" title="Maximilian Ulysses Browne">Maximilian von Browne</a> commanded the Austrian troops. Following the indecisive <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lobositz" title="Battle of Lobositz">Battle of Lobositz</a> in 1756, he was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Charles_Alexander_of_Lorraine" title="Prince Charles Alexander of Lorraine">Prince Charles Alexander of Lorraine</a>, Maria Theresa's brother-in-law.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Frederick was startled by Lobositz; he eventually re-grouped for another attack in June 1757. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kolin" title="Battle of Kolin" class="mw-redirect">Battle of Kolin</a> that followed was a decisive victory for Austria. Frederick lost one third of his troops, and before the battle was over, he had left the scene.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Maria Theresa openly lamented French losses in 1758. France, having secured the Anglo-Hanoverian neutrality for the rest of the conflict,<sup id="cite_ref-Lever.2C_243_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lever.2C_243-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> in September 1757, lost it in January of the next year. That June she suffered a crushing defeat at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Krefeld" title="Battle of Krefeld">Krefeld</a> and French forces withdrew to the Rhine.<sup id="cite_ref-Lever.2C_243_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lever.2C_243-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1759, peace negotiations at <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> came to nothing.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The series of Franco-Austrian losses were reversed until, in 1762, the Empress <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Russia" title="Elizabeth of Russia">Elizabeth of Russia</a> died. Her successor <a href="/wiki/Peter_III_of_Russia" title="Peter III of Russia">Peter III</a> greatly admired Frederick, and at once withdrew Russia's support from the French coalition. Prussia began a drive to expel the Austrians from Saxony, and the French from <a href="/wiki/Landgraviate_of_Hesse-Kassel" title="Landgraviate of Hesse-Kassel">Hesse-Kassel</a>. Though she was only partially successful as her own forces were exhausted, the conflict had essentially descended into a costly stalemate, with Maria Theresa no longer believing that she could retake Silesia. The peace treaties of <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Hubertusburg" title="Treaty of Hubertusburg">Hubertusburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Paris</a> exacted harsh terms from France, as she was forced to relinquish most of her American colonies. For Austria, though, the result was the <a href="/wiki/Status_quo_ante_bellum" title="Status quo ante bellum">status quo ante bellum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-L257_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-L257-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_life">Family life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Family life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresia_Familie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Maria_Theresia_Familie.jpg/220px-Maria_Theresia_Familie.jpg" width="220" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Maria_Theresia_Familie.jpg/330px-Maria_Theresia_Familie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Maria_Theresia_Familie.jpg/440px-Maria_Theresia_Familie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="689" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresia_Familie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maria Theresa with her family, 1754, by Martin van Meytens.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Over the course of twenty years, Maria Theresa gave birth to sixteen children, thirteen of whom survived infancy. The first child, <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Elisabeth_of_Austria_(1737%E2%80%931740)" title="Archduchess Maria Elisabeth of Austria (1737–1740)">Maria Elisabeth</a> (1737–1740), was born a little less than a year after the wedding. Again, the child's gender caused great disappointment and so would the births of <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Anna_of_Austria_(1738%E2%80%931789)" title="Archduchess Maria Anna of Austria (1738–1789)">Maria Anna</a>, the eldest surviving child, and <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Carolina_of_Austria_(1740%E2%80%931741)" title="Archduchess Maria Carolina of Austria (1740–1741)">Maria Carolina</a> (1740–1741). While fighting to preserve her inheritance, Maria Theresa gave birth to a son named after <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph" title="Saint Joseph">Saint Joseph</a>, to whom she had repeatedly prayed for a male child during the pregnancy. Maria Theresa's favourite child, <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Christina,_Duchess_of_Teschen" title="Archduchess Maria Christina, Duchess of Teschen" class="mw-redirect">Maria Christina</a>, was born on her 25th&#160;birthday, four days before the defeat of the Austrian army in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chotusitz" title="Battle of Chotusitz">Chotusitz</a>. Five more children were born during the war: <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Elisabeth_of_Austria_(1743%E2%80%931808)" title="Archduchess Maria Elisabeth of Austria (1743–1808)">Maria Elisabeth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Charles_Joseph_of_Austria_(1745-1761)" title="Archduke Charles Joseph of Austria (1745-1761)" class="mw-redirect">Charles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Amalia_of_Austria" title="Archduchess Maria Amalia of Austria">Maria Amalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Leopold II, Holy Roman Emperor">Leopold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Carolina_of_Austria_(1748)" title="Archduchess Maria Carolina of Austria (1748)">Maria Carolina</a> (1748–1748). During this period, there was no rest for Maria Theresa during pregnancies or around the births; the war and child-bearing were carried on simultaneously. Five children were born during the peace between the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>: <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Johanna_Gabriela_of_Austria" title="Archduchess Maria Johanna Gabriela of Austria">Maria Johanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Josepha_of_Austria" title="Archduchess Maria Josepha of Austria">Maria Josepha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Carolina_of_Austria" title="Maria Carolina of Austria">Maria Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Ferdinand_of_Austria-Este" title="Archduke Ferdinand of Austria-Este" class="mw-redirect">Ferdinand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marie_Antoinette" title="Marie Antoinette">Maria Antonia</a>. She delivered her last child, <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Maximilian_Franz_of_Austria" title="Archduke Maximilian Franz of Austria" class="mw-redirect">Maximilian Francis</a>, during the Seven Years' War, aged 39.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Maria Theresa asserted that, had she not been almost always pregnant, she would have gone into battle herself.<sup id="cite_ref-Holborn.2C_218_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holborn.2C_218-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Maria Theresa's mother, Empress Elisabeth Christine, died in 1750. Four years later, Maria Theresa's governess, Marie Karoline von Fuchs-Mollard, died. The Empress showed her gratitude to Countess Fuchs by having her buried in the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Crypt,_Vienna" title="Imperial Crypt, Vienna" class="mw-redirect">Imperial Crypt</a> along with the members of the imperial family.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahan.2C_22_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahan.2C_22-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after giving birth to the younger children, Maria Theresa was confronted with the task of marrying off the elder ones. She led the marriage negotiations along with the campaigns of her wars and the duties of state. She treated her children with affection but used them as pawns in dynastic games and sacrificed their happiness for the benefit of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-Russell_Richards_Treasure.2C_410_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Russell_Richards_Treasure.2C_410-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> A devoted but self-conscious mother, she wrote to all of her children at least once a week and believed herself entitled to exercise authority over her children regardless of their age and rank.<sup id="cite_ref-Dawson_Beales.2C_194_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dawson_Beales.2C_194-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mariatheresiaoldfamily.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mariatheresiaoldfamily.jpg/220px-Mariatheresiaoldfamily.jpg" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mariatheresiaoldfamily.jpg/330px-Mariatheresiaoldfamily.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mariatheresiaoldfamily.jpg/440px-Mariatheresiaoldfamily.jpg 2x" data-file-width="554" data-file-height="479" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mariatheresiaoldfamily.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The dowager empress with family, 1776, by <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_F%C3%BCger" title="Heinrich Füger">Heinrich Füger</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following her fiftieth birthday in May 1767, Maria Theresa contracted <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> from her daughter-in-law, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Josepha_of_Bavaria" title="Maria Josepha of Bavaria">Maria Josepha of Bavaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> She survived, but the new empress did not. Maria Theresa then forced her daughter, Archduchess Maria Josepha, to pray with her in the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Crypt" title="Imperial Crypt">Imperial Crypt</a> next to the unsealed tomb of Empress Maria Josepha. The Archduchess started showing smallpox rash two days after visiting the crypt and soon died. Maria Carolina was to replace her as the pre-determined bride of King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Ferdinand I of the Two Sicilies">Ferdinand IV of Naples</a>. Maria Theresa blamed herself for her daughter's death for the rest of her life because, at the time, the concept of an extended incubation period was largely unknown and it was believed that Maria Josepha had caught smallpox from the body of the late empress.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In April 1770, Maria Theresa's youngest daughter, Maria Antonia, married <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVI_of_France" title="Louis XVI of France">Louis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dauphin_of_France" title="Dauphin of France">Dauphin of France</a>, by proxy in Vienna. Maria Antonia's education was neglected, and when the French showed an interest in her, her mother went about educating her as best she could about the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Versailles" title="Palace of Versailles">court of Versailles</a> and the French. Maria Theresa kept up a fortnightly correspondence with Maria Antonia, now called Marie Antoinette, in which she often reproached her for laziness and frivolity and scolded her for failing to conceive a child.<sup id="cite_ref-Dawson_Beales.2C_194_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dawson_Beales.2C_194-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Maria Theresa was not just critical of Marie Antoinette. She disliked Leopold's reserve and often blamed him for being cold. She criticised Maria Carolina for her political activities, Ferdinand for his lack of organisation, and Maria Amalia for her poor <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and haughtiness. The only child she did not constantly scold was Maria Christina, who enjoyed her mother's complete confidence, though she failed to please her mother in one aspect – she did not produce any surviving children.<sup id="cite_ref-Dawson_Beales.2C_194_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dawson_Beales.2C_194-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>One of Maria Theresa's greatest wishes was to have as many grandchildren as possible, but she had only about two dozen at the time of her death, of which all the eldest surviving daughters were named after her, with the exception of Caroline of Parma, her eldest granddaughter by Maria Amalia.<sup id="cite_ref-Dawson_Beales.2C_194_104-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dawson_Beales.2C_194-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Issue">Issue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Issue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<tr>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph II</a></b><br />
Holy Roman Emperor</td>
<td>
<p><a href="/wiki/File:Anton_von_Maron_006.png" class="image"><img alt="Anton von Maron 006.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Anton_von_Maron_006.png/100px-Anton_von_Maron_006.png" width="100" height="141" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Anton_von_Maron_006.png/150px-Anton_von_Maron_006.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Anton_von_Maron_006.png/200px-Anton_von_Maron_006.png 2x" data-file-width="346" data-file-height="487" /></a></p>

<td>13 March 1741 -<br />

<td>succeeded his father in the Imperial title but was co-ruler with his mother in the Austrian domains until her death in 1780; married firstly on 6 October 1760 to Princess <a href="/wiki/Princess_Isabella_of_Parma" title="Princess Isabella of Parma">Isabella of Parma</a> and secondly on 23 January 1765 to Princess <a href="/wiki/Maria_Josepha_of_Bavaria" title="Maria Josepha of Bavaria">Maria Josepha of Bavaria</a>. No surviving issue.</td>

<tr>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Leopold_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Leopold II, Holy Roman Emperor">Leopold II</a></b><br />
Holy Roman Emperor</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Johann_Daniel_Donat,_Emperor_Leopold_II_in_the_Regalia_of_the_Golden_Fleece_(1806).png" class="image"><img alt="Johann Daniel Donat, Emperor Leopold II in the Regalia of the Golden Fleece (1806).png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Johann_Daniel_Donat%2C_Emperor_Leopold_II_in_the_Regalia_of_the_Golden_Fleece_%281806%29.png/100px-Johann_Daniel_Donat%2C_Emperor_Leopold_II_in_the_Regalia_of_the_Golden_Fleece_%281806%29.png" width="100" height="155" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Johann_Daniel_Donat%2C_Emperor_Leopold_II_in_the_Regalia_of_the_Golden_Fleece_%281806%29.png/150px-Johann_Daniel_Donat%2C_Emperor_Leopold_II_in_the_Regalia_of_the_Golden_Fleece_%281806%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Johann_Daniel_Donat%2C_Emperor_Leopold_II_in_the_Regalia_of_the_Golden_Fleece_%281806%29.png/200px-Johann_Daniel_Donat%2C_Emperor_Leopold_II_in_the_Regalia_of_the_Golden_Fleece_%281806%29.png 2x" data-file-width="411" data-file-height="639" /></a></td>
