<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_views_and_policies">Religious views and policies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Religious views and policies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresa_of_Austria_family.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Maria_Theresa_of_Austria_family.jpg/220px-Maria_Theresa_of_Austria_family.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Maria_Theresa_of_Austria_family.jpg/330px-Maria_Theresa_of_Austria_family.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Maria_Theresa_of_Austria_family.jpg/440px-Maria_Theresa_of_Austria_family.jpg 2x" data-file-width="590" data-file-height="390" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresa_of_Austria_family.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maria Theresa and her family celebrating <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">Saint Nicholas</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Archduchess_Maria_Christina,_Duchess_of_Teschen" title="Archduchess Maria Christina, Duchess of Teschen" class="mw-redirect">Archduchess Maria Christina</a>, in 1762. The painting depicts the <i>bourgeois</i> cosiness of the imperial family's home.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Like all members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a>, Maria Theresa was a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic" class="mw-redirect">Roman Catholic</a>, and a devout one as well. She believed that religious unity was necessary for a peaceful public life and explicitly rejected the idea of <a href="/wiki/Religious_toleration" title="Religious toleration" class="mw-redirect">religious toleration</a>. However, she never allowed the Church to interfere with what she considered to be prerogatives of a monarch and kept Rome at arm's length. She controlled the selection of archbishops, bishops and abbots.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahan.2C_251_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahan.2C_251-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Her approach to religious piety differed from the approach of her predecessors, as she was influenced by <a href="/wiki/Jansenism" title="Jansenism">Jansenist</a> ideas. The empress actively supported conversion to <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism" class="mw-redirect">Roman Catholicism</a> by securing pensions to the converts. She tolerated <a href="/wiki/Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Greek Catholic Church" class="mw-redirect">Greek Catholics</a> and emphasised their equal status with Roman Catholics.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahan.2C_251_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahan.2C_251-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crankshaw.2C_308_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crankshaw.2C_308-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Besides her devotion to Christianity, she was widely known for her ascetic lifestyle, especially during her 15-year-long widowhood.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jesuits">Jesuits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Jesuits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Her relationship with the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuits</a> was complex. Members of this order educated her, served as her confessors, and supervised the religious education of her eldest son. The Jesuits were powerful and influential in the early years of Maria Theresa's reign. However, the queen's ministers convinced her that the order posed a danger to her monarchical authority. Not without much hesitation and regret, she issued a decree which removed them from all the institutions of the monarchy, and carried it out thoroughly. She forbade the publication of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_XIII" title="Pope Clement XIII">Pope Clement XIII</a>'s bull which was in favour of the Jesuits and promptly confiscated their property when <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_XIV" title="Pope Clement XIV">Pope Clement XIV</a> suppressed the order.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahan.2C_254_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahan.2C_254-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jews_and_Protestants">Jews and Protestants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Jews and Protestants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Though she eventually gave up trying to convert her non-Catholic subjects to Roman Catholicism, Maria Theresa regarded both the <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants" class="mw-redirect">Protestants</a> as dangerous to the state and actively tried to suppress them.<sup id="cite_ref-DB2_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB2-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> The empress was probably the most <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">anti-Semitic</a> monarch of her time, having inherited the traditional prejudices of her ancestors and acquired new ones. This was a product of deep religious devotion and was not kept secret in her time.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1777, she wrote of the Jews: "I know of no greater plague than this race, which on account of its deceit, usury and avarice is driving my subjects into beggary. Therefore as far as possible, the Jews are to be kept away and avoided."<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>She imposed extremely harsh taxes on her Jewish subjects and, in December 1744, proposed expelling the Jews from her hereditary dominions to her ministers. Her first intention was to expel all Jews by 1&#160;January, but having accepted the advice of her ministers who were concerned by the number of future expellees, had them expelled by June. She also transferred Protestants from Austria to <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a> and cut down the number of religious holidays and monastic orders. In 1777, she abandoned the idea of expelling Moravian Protestants after Joseph, who was opposed to her intentions, threatened to abdicate as emperor and co-ruler. Finally, she was forced to grant them some toleration by allowing them to worship privately. Joseph regarded his mother's religious policies as "unjust, impious, impossible, harmful and ridiculous".<sup id="cite_ref-Mahan.2C_254_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahan.2C_254-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DB2_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB2-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Holborn.2C_222_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holborn.2C_222-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the third decade of her reign, influenced by her Jewish courtier <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Mendel_Theben" title="Abraham Mendel Theben">Abraham Mendel Theben</a>, Maria Theresa issued edicts which offered some state protection to her Jewish subjects. She forbade the forcible conversion of Jewish children to Christianity in 1762. In 1763, she forbade Catholic clergy from extracting <a href="/wiki/Surplice_fees" title="Surplice fees">surplice fees</a> from her Jewish subjects. In 1764, she ordered the release of those Jews who had been jailed for a <a href="/wiki/Blood_libel" title="Blood libel">blood libel</a> in the village of Orkuta. Notwithstanding her strong dislike of Jews, Maria Theresa supported Jewish commercial and industrial activity.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reforms">Reforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Reforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresia11.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Maria_Theresia11.jpg/220px-Maria_Theresia11.jpg" width="220" height="332" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Maria_Theresia11.jpg/330px-Maria_Theresia11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Maria_Theresia11.jpg 2x" data-file-width="398" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresia11.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Maria Theresa</i> in 1762, by <a href="/wiki/Jean-%C3%89tienne_Liotard" title="Jean-Étienne Liotard">Jean-Étienne Liotard</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Maria Theresa was as conservative in manners of state as in those of religion, but implemented significant reforms to strengthen Austria's military and bureaucratic efficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-Byrne.2C_38_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrne.2C_38-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> She employed <a href="/wiki/Count_Friedrich_Wilhelm_von_Haugwitz" title="Count Friedrich Wilhelm von Haugwitz">Count Friedrich Wilhelm von Haugwitz</a>, who modernised the empire by creating a standing army of 108,000&#160;men, paid for with 14&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_gulden" title="Austro-Hungarian gulden">gulden</a> extracted from each crown-land. The central government was responsible for the army, although Haugwitz instituted taxation of the nobility, who never before had to pay taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Maria Theresa oversaw the unification of the Austrian and Bohemian chancellories in May 1749.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Maria Theresa doubled the state revenue between 1754 and 1764, though her attempt to tax clergy and nobility was only partially successful.<sup id="cite_ref-Byrne.2C_38_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrne.2C_38-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-C195_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C195-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> These financial reforms greatly improved the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1760, Maria Theresa created the council of state, composed of the state chancellor, three members of the high nobility and three knights, which served as a committee of experienced people who advised her. The council of state lacked executive or legislative authority, but nevertheless showed the difference between the form of government employed by Frederick II of Prussia. Unlike the latter, Maria Theresa was not an autocrat who acted as her own minister. Prussia would adopt this form of government only after 1807.<sup id="cite_ref-Holborn.2C_222_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holborn.2C_222-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medicine_and_Hygiene">Medicine and Hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Medicine and Hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gerard_van_Swieten" title="Gerard van Swieten">Gerard van Swieten</a>, whom Maria Theresa had recruited following the death of her sister, Archduchess Maria Anna, founded the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_General_Hospital" title="Vienna General Hospital">Vienna General Hospital</a>, revamped Austria's educational system and served as the Empress's personal physician. After calling in van Swieten, Maria Theresa asked him to study the problem of infant mortality in Austria. Following his recommendation, she made a decree that autopsies would be mandatory for all hospital deaths in the city of Graz, Austria's second largest city. This law – still in effect today – combined with the relatively stable population of Graz, resulted in one of the most important and complete autopsy records in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-unsuspectill_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unsuspectill-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-riddleillness_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riddleillness-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Maria Theresa banned the creation of new burial grounds without prior government permission, thus countering wasteful and unhygienic burial customs.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Her decision to have her children <a href="/wiki/Inoculation" title="Inoculation">inoculated</a> after the smallpox epidemic of 1767 was responsible for changing Austrian physicians' negative view of inoculation.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> The empress herself inaugurated inoculation in Austria by hosting a dinner for the first sixty-five inoculated children in <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nbrunn_Palace" title="Schönbrunn Palace">Schönbrunn Palace</a>, waiting on the children herself.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_rights">Civil rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Civil rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Among other reforms was the <i>Codex Theresianus</i>, begun in 1752 and finished in 1766, that defined civil rights.<sup id="cite_ref-C195_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C195-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1776, Austria outlawed <a href="/wiki/Witch-hunt" title="Witch-hunt">witch burnings</a> and torture. It was later reintroduced, but the progressive nature of these reforms remains noted. Much unlike Joseph, but with the support of religious authorities, Maria Theresa was opposed to the abolition of torture. Born and raised between <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">Rococo</a> eras, she found it hard to fit into the intellectual sphere of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a>, which is why she only slowly followed humanitarian reforms on the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Church">Church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>She is most unusually ambitious and hopes to make the House of Austria more renowned than it has ever been.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>Prussian ambassador's letter to <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II_of_Prussia" title="Frederick II of Prussia" class="mw-redirect">Frederick II of Prussia</a><sup id="cite_ref-Mahan.2C_230_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahan.2C_230-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>That woman's achievements are those of a great man.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>The writings of Frederick II of Prussia<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>Main reforms concerning the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church" class="mw-redirect">Roman Catholic Church</a> were initiated and carried out under Maria Theresa, while the reforms under her son concerned their non-Catholic subjects. The ecclesiastical policies of Maria Theresa, like those of her devout predecessors, were based not on anti-religious principles, but on ensuring primacy of State control in Church-State relations.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aware of the inadequacy of bureaucracy in Austria and, in order to improve it, Maria Theresa reformed education in 1775. In a new school system based on the Prussian one, all children of both genders from the ages of six to twelve had to attend school. Education reform was met with hostility from many villages; Maria Theresa crushed the dissent by ordering the arrest of all those opposed. Although the idea had merit, the reforms were not as successful as they were expected to be; in some parts of Austria, half of the population was illiterate well into the 19th&#160;century.<sup id="cite_ref-Holborn.2C_222_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holborn.2C_222-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The empress permitted non-Catholics to attend university and allowed the introduction of secular subjects (such as law), which influenced the decline of <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theology</a> as the main foundation of university education.<sup id="cite_ref-Crankshaw.2C_308_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crankshaw.2C_308-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Byrne.2C_38_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrne.2C_38-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_reign">Late reign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Late reign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anton_von_Maron_005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Anton_von_Maron_005.jpg/170px-Anton_von_Maron_005.jpg" width="170" height="374" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Anton_von_Maron_005.jpg/255px-Anton_von_Maron_005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Anton_von_Maron_005.jpg/340px-Anton_von_Maron_005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="807" data-file-height="1775" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anton_von_Maron_005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maria Theresa as a widow in 1773, by <a href="/wiki/Anton_von_Maron" title="Anton von Maron">Anton von Maron</a>. <i>Peace</i> holds the <a href="/wiki/Olive_branch" title="Olive branch">olive crown</a> above her head, reaffirming Maria Theresa's monarchical status. This was the last commissioned state portrait of Maria Theresa.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Emperor Francis died on 18 August 1765, while he and the court were in <a href="/wiki/Innsbruck" title="Innsbruck">Innsbruck</a> celebrating the wedding of his second son, Leopold. Maria Theresa was devastated. Their eldest son, Joseph, became Holy Roman Emperor. Maria Theresa abandoned all ornamentation, had her hair cut short, painted her rooms black and dressed in mourning for the rest of her life. She completely withdrew from court life, public events, and theater. Throughout her widowhood, she spent the whole August and the eighteenth of each month alone in her chamber, which negatively affected her mental health.<sup id="cite_ref-Cr267_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cr267-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> She described her state of mind shortly after Francis's death: "I hardly know myself now, for I have become like an animal with no true life or reasoning power."<sup id="cite_ref-Cr267_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cr267-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Upon his accession to the imperial throne, Joseph ruled less land than his father had in 1740. Believing that the emperor must possess enough land to maintain the Empire's integrity, Maria Theresa, who was used to being assisted in the administration of her vast realms, declared Joseph to be her new co-ruler on 17 September 1765.<sup id="cite_ref-Dawson_Beales.2C_136_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dawson_Beales.2C_136-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> From then on, mother and son had frequent ideological disagreements.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The 22&#160;million gulden that Joseph inherited from his father was injected into the treasury. Maria Theresa had another loss in February 1766 when Haugwitz died. She gave her son absolute control over the military following the death of <a href="/wiki/Count_Leopold_Joseph_von_Daun" title="Count Leopold Joseph von Daun">Count Leopold Joseph von Daun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to Robert A. Kann, Maria Theresa was a monarch of above-average qualifications but intellectually inferior to Joseph and Leopold.<sup id="cite_ref-Kann.2C_157_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kann.2C_157-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> He asserts that she nevertheless possessed qualities appreciated in a monarch: warm heart, practical mind, firm determination and sound perception. Most importantly, she was ready to recognise the mental superiority of some of her advisers and to give way to a superior mind while enjoying support of her ministers even if their ideas differed from her own. Joseph, however, was never able to establish rapport with the same advisers, even though their philosophy of government was closer to Joseph's than to Maria Theresa's.<sup id="cite_ref-Kann.2C_157_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kann.2C_157-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:30em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>She never bothers about her health, but relies entirely upon her vigorous body for strength and endurance. She is warm-blooded and, even in the middle of winter, often sits by an open window ... Her physician scolds her dreadfully about this, but she only laughs at him.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>Prussian ambassador's letter to <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a>, c. 1748<sup id="cite_ref-Mahan.2C_230_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahan.2C_230-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>The relationship between Maria Theresa and Joseph was not without warmth but was complicated and their personalities clashed. Despite his intellect, Maria Theresa's force of personality often made Joseph cower. Sometimes, she openly admired his talents and achievements, but criticised him behind his back.<sup id="cite_ref-DB1_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB1-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> She wrote: "We never see each other except at dinner ... His temper gets worse every day ... Please burn this letter ... I just try to avoid public scandal."<sup id="cite_ref-DB1_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB1-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> In another letter, also addressed to Joseph's companion, she complained: "He avoids me ... I am the only person in his way and so I am an obstruction and a burden ... Abdication alone can remedy matters."<sup id="cite_ref-DB1_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB1-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After much contemplation, she chose not to abdicate. Joseph himself often threatened to resign as co-regent and emperor, but he, too, was induced not to do so. Her threats of abdication were rarely taken seriously; Maria Theresa believed that her recovery from smallpox in 1767 was a sign that God wished her to reign until death. It was in Joseph's interest that she remained sovereign, for he often blamed her for his failures and thus avoided taking on the responsibilities of a monarch.<sup id="cite_ref-DB1_141-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB1-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Joseph and Prince Kaunitz arranged the <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">First Partition of Poland</a> despite Maria Theresa's protestations. Her sense of justice pushed her to reject the idea of partition, which would hurt the <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Polish people</a>. The duo argued that it was too late to abort now. Besides, Maria Theresa herself agreed with the partition when she realised that <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II_of_Prussia" title="Frederick II of Prussia" class="mw-redirect">Frederick II of Prussia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catherine_II_of_Russia" title="Catherine II of Russia" class="mw-redirect">Catherine II of Russia</a> would do it with or without Austrian participation. Maria Theresa claimed and eventually took <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia_and_Lodomeria" title="Kingdom of Galicia and Lodomeria">Galicia and Lodomeria</a>, a province claimed by Hungarian monarchs since the 13th&#160;century; in the words of Frederick, "the more she cried, the more she took".<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_and_legacy">Death and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Death and legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kaisergruft_2286201074_fdea9c4cfa_b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Kaisergruft_2286201074_fdea9c4cfa_b.jpg/170px-Kaisergruft_2286201074_fdea9c4cfa_b.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Kaisergruft_2286201074_fdea9c4cfa_b.jpg/255px-Kaisergruft_2286201074_fdea9c4cfa_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Kaisergruft_2286201074_fdea9c4cfa_b.jpg/340px-Kaisergruft_2286201074_fdea9c4cfa_b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kaisergruft_2286201074_fdea9c4cfa_b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maria Theresa and her husband are interred in the double tomb which she had inscribed as a widow.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>It is unlikely that Maria Theresa ever completely recovered from the <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> attack in 1767, as 18th-century writers asserted. She suffered from <a href="/wiki/Shortness_of_breath" title="Shortness of breath" class="mw-redirect">shortness of breath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatigue_(medical)" title="Fatigue (medical)">fatigue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cough" title="Cough">cough</a>, distress, <a href="/wiki/Necrophobia" title="Necrophobia">necrophobia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Insomnia" title="Insomnia">insomnia</a>. She later developed <a href="/wiki/Edema" title="Edema">edema</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The empress fell ill on 24 November 1780, ostensibly of a chill. Her physician Dr. Störk thought her condition serious. By 28&#160;November, she asked for the <a href="/wiki/Anointing_of_the_Sick_(Catholic_Church)" title="Anointing of the Sick (Catholic Church)">last rites</a>, and the next day, at about nine o'clock in the evening, she died surrounded by her remaining children. With her, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a> died out and was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lorraine" title="House of Lorraine">House of Habsburg-Lorraine</a>. Joseph, already co-sovereign of the Habsburg dominions, succeeded her.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After several diplomatic failures and military defeats in the 1730s, Austria seemed to be declining, or even on the verge of collapse. After her forty years reign, Maria Theresa left a revitalised empire that influenced the rest of Europe throughout the 19th&#160;century. She gave the Habsburg dominions an efficient administrative system that allowed it to remain a great power in its own right, without the support of the Holy Roman Empire. Her descendants followed her example and continued reforming the empire. The acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia_and_Lodomeria" title="Kingdom of Galicia and Lodomeria">Kingdom of Galicia and Lodomeria</a> gave the empire an even more multinational character that would ultimately lead to its destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Her introduction of compulsory schooling, as a means of <a href="/wiki/Germanisation" title="Germanisation">Germanisation</a>, eventually triggered the revival of Czech culture.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The empress is buried in the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Crypt,_Vienna" title="Imperial Crypt, Vienna" class="mw-redirect">Imperial Crypt</a> in Vienna next to her husband in a coffin she had inscribed during her lifetime.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Full_title">Full title</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Full title">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="floatleft"><a href="/wiki/File:Middle_Coat_of_Arms_of_Maria_Theresa,_Holy_Roman_Empress.svg" class="image" title="Coat of arms of Maria Theresa"><img alt="Coat of arms of Maria Theresa" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Middle_Coat_of_Arms_of_Maria_Theresa%2C_Holy_Roman_Empress.svg/100px-Middle_Coat_of_Arms_of_Maria_Theresa%2C_Holy_Roman_Empress.svg.png" width="100" height="138" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Middle_Coat_of_Arms_of_Maria_Theresa%2C_Holy_Roman_Empress.svg/150px-Middle_Coat_of_Arms_of_Maria_Theresa%2C_Holy_Roman_Empress.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Middle_Coat_of_Arms_of_Maria_Theresa%2C_Holy_Roman_Empress.svg/200px-Middle_Coat_of_Arms_of_Maria_Theresa%2C_Holy_Roman_Empress.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="919" data-file-height="1271" /></a></div>
<p>Her title after the death of her husband was:</p>
<p><i>Maria Theresa, <a href="/wiki/By_the_Grace_of_God" title="By the Grace of God">by the Grace of God</a>, Dowager Empress of the Romans, Queen of Hungary, of Bohemia, of Dalmatia, of Croatia, of Slavonia, of Galicia, of Lodomeria, etc.; Archduchess of Austria; Duchess of Burgundy, of Styria, of Carinthia and of Carniola; Grand Princess of Transylvania; Margravine of Moravia; Duchess of Brabant, of Limburg, of Luxemburg, of Guelders, of Württemberg, of Upper and Lower Silesia, of Milan, of Mantua, of Parma, of Piacenza, of Guastalla, of Auschwitz and of Zator; Princess of Swabia; Princely Countess of Habsburg, of Flanders, of Tyrol, of Hainault, of Kyburg, of Gorizia and of Gradisca; Margravine of Burgau, of Upper and Lower Lusatia; Countess of Namur; Lady of the Wendish Mark and of Mechlin; Dowager Duchess of Lorraine and Bar, Dowager Grand Duchess of Tuscany.</i><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Theresa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ancestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As she was the second Maria to reign over the Austrian Netherlands (after <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Burgundy" title="Mary of Burgundy">Mary the Rich</a>) and Hungary (after <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Hungary" title="Mary of Hungary" class="mw-redirect">Mary of Anjou</a>), she is sometimes listed as <b>Maria&#160;II Theresa</b>. Ellenius, 210.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Britannica-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Britannica_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Britannica_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/364907/Maria-Theresa">Marie Theresa</a>. <li id="cite_note-Kann.2C_157-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Kann.2C_157_5-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Kann.2C_157_5-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Kann.2C_157_5-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Kann.2C_157_5-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Kann, 157.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Browning.2C_67-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Browning.2C_67_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Browning.2C_67_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Browning, 67.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In a letter to Joseph, the Empress wrote: "What, without a dominant religion? Toleration, indifferentism, are exactly the right means to undermine everything... What other restraint exists? None. Neither the <a href="/wiki/Gallows" title="Gallows">gallows</a> nor the <a href="/wiki/Breaking_wheel" title="Breaking wheel">wheel</a>... I speak politically now, not as a Christian. Nothing is so necessary and beneficial as religion. Would you allow everyone to act according to his fantasy? If there were no fixed cult, no subjection to the Church, where should we be? The law of might would take command." Crankshaw, 302.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Dawson Beales, 69.</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Maria Theresa survived both her sisters. Maria Amalia died at the age of six, while Maria Anna died in childbirth in 1744. Ingrao, 128.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mahan, 23.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mahan, 228.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Members of the Habsburg dynasty often married their close relatives; examples of such inbreeding were uncle-niece pairs (Maria Theresa's grandfather <a href="/wiki/Leopold_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Leopold I, Holy Roman Emperor">Leopold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Theresa_of_Spain" title="Margaret Theresa of Spain">Margaret Theresa of Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anna_of_Austria_(1549%E2%80%931580)" title="Anna of Austria (1549–1580)" class="mw-redirect">Anna of Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_Spain" title="Philip IV of Spain">Philip IV of Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mariana_of_Austria" title="Mariana of Austria">Mariana of Austria</a>, etc). Maria Theresa, however, descended from Leopold I's third wife who was not closely related to him, and her parents were only distantly related. Dawson Beales, 21.</span></li>

Spielman, 206.</span></li>
